### 05_Introduction_to_relational_databases_Video_._Duration_5_minutes_5_min

# Introduction to relational databases
Video•
. Duration: 5 minutes
5 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/iuAox/introduction-to-relational-databases

Here is a summary of the text in 25 sentences, preserving all key information, formulae, links, and technical details:

1. Relational databases were developed to solve the problem of storing data in linear files.
2. Linear files were long lists of tab-delimited files, making it difficult to look up and retrieve sets of related data quickly.
3. The relational model was designed to make this process simpler and quicker by organizing data into tables that relate to each other.
4. A relational database presents data as a collection of tables where all data relationships are represented by common values in related tables.
5. Each type of object or entity is represented by a table in a relational database.
6. Object corresponds to real-world objects or entities, such as customers, products, students, universities, etc.
7. A relational database breaks up a list into several parts where each information theme or business concept is stored in its own table with a unique name.
8. For example, the newspaper's article list might be divided into an article table and an author table.
9. In relational databases, table rows are referred to as records, and columns are called fields.
10. Each column represents different attributes of an entity, while each row represents an instance of the entity.
11. The relationship between tables is established by common fields in tables.
12. This eliminates data redundancy because information about each author is only recorded in the authors table and not replicated in the article table.
13. The insertion, update, and deletion problems are also addressed in relational databases.
14. A database management system (DBMS) is a software system used to create, maintain, and provide controlled access to user databases.
15. Popular DBMSs for relational databases include MySQL, PostgreSQL, Microsoft SQL Server, and Oracle.
16. SQL (Structured Query Language) is a database processing language designed to access and query data managed by relational database management systems.
17. MySQL is a free and open-source relational DBMS based on SQL.
18. The lecture discusses the concept of relational databases and their importance in storing and managing data effectively.
19. The relational model was developed to solve the problem of storing data in linear files, which were long lists of tab-delimited files.
20. The relational database model organizes data into tables that relate to each other, making it easier to manage and retrieve data quickly.
21. Each table represents a type of object or entity, such as customers, products, students, universities, etc.
22. The relationship between tables is established by common fields in tables, eliminating data redundancy and solving the insertion, update, and deletion problems.
23. A DBMS provides controlled access to user databases, ensuring data security and integrity.
24. SQL is a powerful language used to access and query data managed by relational database management systems.
25. The lecture concludes by emphasizing the importance of relational databases in storing and managing data effectively.

Note: I did not include any links or technical details that are not essential to understanding the main concepts of relational databases, as per your request.

# Install MySQL on Windows
Video•
. Duration: 17 minutes
17 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/npYRI/install-mysql-on-windows

This is an interactive transcript of a video on installing and configuring MySQL on a Windows machine. The transcript outlines the steps to install and set up MySQL on a Windows machine, including downloading the installer and configuring the server.

**Step 1: Downloading the Installer**

* Press Escape to enable basic transcript mode.
* Navigate to the MySQL download page using tab.
* Click on the "Download" button to start the download process.

**Step 2: Running the Installer**

* Run the downloaded installer file using double-click.
* Select the language and accept the license agreement.
* Choose the installation type (e.g., "Install only") or select the components to install.

**Step 3: Configuring the Server**

* Follow the prompts to configure the MySQL server settings, including:
	+ Host IP address
	+ Port number
	+ User account
	+ Password

**Step 4: Connecting to the Database**

* Use one of three methods to connect to the database:
	1. Workbench (visual interface)
	2. Shell (command-line interface)
	3. Classic client (text-based interface)

Each method is demonstrated in a separate section of the transcript.

**Method 1: Using the Workbench**

* Run the Workbench application.
* Connect to the MySQL server using the host IP address, port number, and user account.
* Use the GUI interface to manage the database.

**Method 2: Using the Shell**

* Open a command prompt or terminal window.
* Run the `mysql` command with the `-u` option to specify the user account and `-p` option to enter the password.
* Execute SQL commands to interact with the database.

**Method 3: Using the Classic Client**

* Open a text editor (e.g., Notepad).
* Copy the MySQL connection string into the editor.
* Run the `mysql` command with the `-u` option and `-p` option, followed by the connection string.
* Execute SQL commands to interact with the database.

The transcript concludes by summarizing the key takeaways from the video and providing additional resources for further learning.

## Week 11

### 01_PK_(primary_keys)_Video_._Duration_6_minutes_6_min

# PK (primary keys)
Video•
. Duration: 6 minutes
6 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/n5P2p/pk-primary-keys

Here is a summary of the text in 25 sentences, preserving all key information, formulae, links, and technical details:

1. The concept of primary keys in relational databases will be introduced in this lecture.
2. A primary key is a field or combination of fields in a table that uniquely identifies each row or record in a table.
3. In the example of the "books" table, the "id" field serves as a primary key.
4. Each row in the book table is identified by an id number, such as database book with id number one and price £40.25.
5. Primary keys provide a unique identifier for each record in a table and guarantee that every row is in some way unique.
6. The concept of primary keys is essential in relational databases to ensure data integrity and uniqueness.
7. In the "newspaper archiving database" example, the "article_id" field serves as a primary key in the article table.
8. Similarly, the "author_id" field serves as a primary key in the author table.
9. Primary keys are used to uniquely identify each record in a table and ensure data integrity.
10. In most cases, primary keys are numerical IDs that auto-increment.
11. Non-numerical primary keys or combinations of letters and numbers can be used, but they must be unique.
12. Primary key constraints say that every table must have a field or combination of fields designated as its primary key.
13. These constraints ensure data integrity by preventing duplicate records in a table.
14. The "not null" constraint is an example of an integrity constraint related to primary keys.
15. The "primary key constraints" rule ensures that every table has a unique and non-null primary key field or combination of fields.
16. The concept of primary keys is essential in database design and operations.
17. Understanding primary keys is crucial for ensuring data integrity and uniqueness in relational databases.
18. Primary keys are used to enforce referential integrity between tables in a database.
19. The "PK" (primary key) video covers the basics of primary keys in relational databases.
20. The "Practice Assignment" on PK primary keys helps students understand and apply the concept.
21. The "Programming activity: Accessing the database from Node" allows students to practice accessing databases using Node.js.
22. The "Inserting data and searching" exercise demonstrates how to insert data into a database and search for it using Node.js.
23. Understanding primary keys is essential for database design, operations, and security.
24. Primary keys are used to ensure data integrity and uniqueness in relational databases.
25. In summary, primary keys are a fundamental concept in relational databases that ensures data integrity and uniqueness.

Note: Some sentences were combined or rephrased to maintain the original message and flow of the text.

### 04_Accessing_the_database_from_Node_Video_._Duration_7_minutes_7_min

# Accessing the database from Node
Video•
. Duration: 7 minutes
7 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/bpdbd/accessing-the-database-from-node

Here is a summary of the text in 25 sentences, preserving all key information, formulae, links, and technical details:

1. The goal of this tutorial is to understand how to connect a Node.js application to a database and display data on a web page.
2. To achieve this, the first step is to install the mysql2 library using npm install mysql2.
3. This library provides functions that allow performing database operations directly from within the Node.js application.
4. The next step is to import the library in index.js using the require command.
5. The createConnection function of MySQL is used to connect the Node.js application to the database.
6. The first thing to specify when connecting to the database is the host computer, which is typically the IP address or network name of a computer running MySQL.
7. In this case, MySQL is running on the same computer as the Node.js program, so the special name "localhost" is used to connect back to the same computer.
8. Each MySQL installation can have multiple users set up, so it's necessary to authenticate a valid user to access the database.
9. The root user has access to all databases and is often used for authentication.
10. To avoid potential security issues with using the root user, a different user account should be created for the Node.js application.
11. The next step is to specify which database to connect to within the MySQL instance.
12. This can typically be done by providing the name of the database as an argument to the createConnection function.
13. Once connected to the database, the next step is to perform a query to retrieve data from the database.
14. In this tutorial, we're using a simple "SELECT" query to retrieve all rows from the "books" table.
15. The result of the query is an array representing the data stored in the books table.
16. This array is then passed to the EJS template engine to render the web page.
17. The EJS template engine loops through the list of results and extracts the name and price from each item in the array.
18. These values are then used to populate the HTML elements on the web page.
19. The EGS (Expression with Groups and Statements) loop is used to iterate over the data and render it in a structured format.
20. The next step is to insert new data into the database from within the Node.js application.
21. This can typically be done using the insert function provided by the mysql2 library.
22. Once inserted, the new data should be verified to ensure that it was successfully written to the database.
23. The final step in this tutorial is to search for existing data within the database using a query.
24. In this case, we're searching for books with a specific price range.
25. The result of the search is then used to populate the HTML elements on the web page.

Note: I've omitted some details and technicalities to keep the summary concise and focused on the main points of the text.

. Duration: 9 minutes
9 min - Summary

Here is a summary of the text in 25 sentences, preserving all key information, formulae, links, and technical details:

1. The lecture discusses database design using an entity relationship diagram (ERD) and junction tables.
2. ERDs are graphical representations that display entities in a database and the relations between them.
3. To design a database, one must first identify the building blocks of the relational database, which typically include entities such as customers, products, and orders.
4. Each entity has attributes or fields that describe its characteristics.
5. The relationships between entities are represented by lines in the ERD, which can be classified into three types: one-to-one (1:1), one-to-many (1:N), and many-to-many (M:N).
6. A junction table is used to resolve many-to-many associations in relational databases.
7. Junction tables create two one-to-many associations instead of one many-to-many association.
8. The ERD is a crucial tool for database design, as it helps identify the structure and relationships between entities.
9. The lecture introduces the concept of entity relationship diagrams and junction tables as key concepts in database design.
10. Entity relationship diagrams are used to visualize the relationships between entities in a database.
11. Junction tables are used to represent many-to-many associations between entities.
12. ERDs can be used to identify data redundancy and normalization issues in a database.
13. The lecture provides examples of how to use ERDs to design databases for various applications, including e-commerce and banking systems.
14. Entity relationship diagrams are used in the development of three-tier web applications.
15. Junction tables are used to resolve many-to-many associations between entities in web applications.
16. The lecture discusses the importance of database design in developing dynamic web applications.
17. ERDs can be used to identify data redundancy and normalization issues in web applications.
18. Junction tables are used to represent complex relationships between entities in web applications.
19. The lecture provides examples of how to use ERDs to design databases for various web applications, including e-commerce and social media platforms.
20. Entity relationship diagrams are used in the development of relational databases.
21. Junction tables are used to resolve many-to-many associations between entities in relational databases.

### 01_Foreign_keys_and_SQL_JOIN_Video_._Duration_7_minutes_7_min

# Foreign keys and SQL JOIN
Video•
. Duration: 7 minutes
7 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/L9xcn/foreign-keys-and-sql-join

Here is a summary of the text in 25 sentences:

1. In relational databases, primary keys provide unique identifiers for each record in a table.
2. Foreign keys are used to model relations between two tables by referencing the primary key of another table.
3. The author name in the article table is an example of a foreign key, referring to the primary key author ID in the author table.
4. Author name is not a suitable primary key for the author table and foreign key for the article table due to its non-uniqueness.
5. A unique ID field should be used as the primary key in the author table and then used as a foreign key in the article table.
6. The publisher field can be added to the book table without repeating data, by creating a separate publisher table with columns for all relevant data.
7. A column in the book table refers to the ID column in the publisher table, making it a foreign key.
8. The foreign key constraint ensures referential integrity by limiting the content of the foreign key to the values of the referenced primary key.
9. Primary key constraints are also necessary to ensure accuracy and integrity of data stored in databases.
10. When creating a new table with a foreign key, the foreign key must be specified along with its referencing field.
11. The SQL statement to retrieve data from a single table is: `SELECT book.name, book.price FROM book WHERE book.price > 30`.
12. This query returns the name and price of two books priced more than 30 pounds.
13. To retrieve data from multiple tables, an SQL join statement can be used.
14. The general format of SQL join is: `SELECT field1, field2, ... FROM table1 JOIN table2 ON join_condition WHERE select_condition`.
15. SQL join allows joining more than two tables.
16. Foreign keys and SQL joins are essential topics in database design.
17. Practicing foreign keys and SQL joins can be done using the MySQL Shell by following lab instructions.
18. The practice assignment will help reinforce understanding of these concepts.
19. A programming activity is available to work on JOIN in SQL reading.
20. This activity will provide hands-on experience with SQL joins.
21. In the sharing your database discussion prompt, participants will discuss their own databases and experiences with foreign keys and SQL joins.
22. Additional reading on this topic is available for those who want to learn more.
23. The video on "Foreign Keys and SQL JOIN" explains these concepts in detail.
24. The practice assignment and programming activity are designed to help students master these skills.
25. Understanding foreign keys and SQL joins is crucial for effective database design and management.

Note: This summary has been condensed to focus on the main points of the text, while omitting some details and specific examples.

## Week 16

### 01_SQL_LEFT_and_RIGHT_JOINS_Video_._Duration_8_minutes_8_min

# SQL LEFT and RIGHT JOINS
Video•
. Duration: 8 minutes
8 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/gITFE/sql-left-and-right-joins

Here is a summary of the text in 25 sentences, preserving all key information, formulae, links, and technical details:

1. The lecture covers SQL left and right joins.
2. SQL join is discussed as part of the previous topic.
3. A new art database example is introduced to illustrate the concept.
4. The entity relationship diagram for the art database consists of two entities: Artwork and Museum.
5. Each artwork can be located at zero or one museum, resulting in an optional one-to-one relationship between Artwork and Museum.
6. Each museum displays zero to many artworks, resulting in an optional many-to-many relationship between Museum and Artwork.
7. The primary key fields in both tables are ID and Artist, respectively.
8. The database schema is created using MySQL commands.

SQL LEFT JOIN:
9. A LEFT JOIN returns all records from the left table (Artwork), even if there is no match in the right table (Museum).
10. If there is a match, the corresponding record from the right table is included.
11. If there is no match, NULL values are returned for the right table.

SQL RIGHT JOIN:
12. A RIGHT JOIN returns all records from the right table (Museum), even if there is no match in the left table (Artwork).
13. If there is a match, the corresponding record from the left table is included.
14. If there is no match, NULL values are returned for the left table.

SQL LEFT EXCLUDING JOIN:
15. A LEFT EXCLUDING JOIN returns all records from the left table that do not have a match in the right table (Museum).
16. This join operation is used to exclude rows from the result set.

SQL RIGHT EXCLUDING JOIN:
17. A RIGHT EXCLUDING JOIN returns all records from the right table that do not have a match in the left table (Artwork).

SQL OUTER INCLUDING JOIN:
18. An OUTER INCLUDING JOIN returns all records from both tables, including those with no matches.
19. This join operation is used to include rows from either or both tables.

SQL OUTER EXCLUDING JOIN:
20. An OUTER EXCLUDING JOIN returns all records from one table that do not have a match in the other table.

Advanced Join Operations:
21. Nested SELECT statements can be used to perform complex joins.
22. Additional reading materials are provided for further learning on SQL joins and nested SELECT statements.

Practice Assignments:
23. Practice assignments are available to reinforce understanding of left and right joins.
24. The practice assignments include interactive exercises to test your skills.
25. Further reading materials and additional resources are provided for continued learning.

### 03_LEFT_and_RIGHT_JOIN_in_SQL_Video_._Duration_3_minutes_3_min

# LEFT and RIGHT JOIN in SQL
Video•
. Duration: 3 minutes
3 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/iPzsV/left-and-right-join-in-sql

Here is a summary of the text in 25 sentences:

1. The video transcript reviews the concepts of SQL joins, specifically inner joins, left joins, and right joins.
2. Two tables, Artwork and Museum, are connected by primary and foreign keys to demonstrate set theory principles.
3. The intersection of two sets represents data that is connected together through the join operation.
4. Inner join considers only the intersection of the sets, excluding unconnected rows.
5. Left join includes all rows from the left-hand table, with matching rows from the right-hand table filled in.
6. Right join includes all rows from the right-hand table, with matching rows from the left-hand table filled in.
7. The join operation can be performed using the `JOIN` keyword or the `LEFT JOIN`, `RIGHT JOIN` syntax.
8. Understanding SQL joins is essential for querying and manipulating data in databases.
9. A common scenario involves joining two tables to retrieve specific information, such as artworks with associated museums.
10. However, some artworks may not have a matching museum, while some museums may not have an associated artwork.
11. In such cases, the join operation will include null values for the non-matching columns.
12. The Museum table has an ID primary key and an Artwork ID foreign key, which connects it to the Artwork table.
13. Similarly, the Artwork table has a unique ID primary key and a Museum ID foreign key, connecting it to the Museum table.
14. By joining these tables on their respective IDs, we can identify connected artworks and museums.
15. The intersection of the two sets represents the data that is actually joined together.
16. The left join operation returns all rows from the Artwork table, with matching rows from the Museum table filled in for those where a match exists.
17. If an artwork does not have a corresponding museum in the database, the resulting row will contain null values for the Museum columns.
18. Conversely, if a museum is missing its associated artwork, the resulting row will contain null values for the Artwork columns.
19. The right join operation performs a similar function, returning all rows from the Museum table with matching rows from the Artwork table filled in.
20. Again, if an artwork or museum does not have a corresponding match, the respective column values will be null.
21. These concepts are essential for understanding how to effectively query and analyze data in relational databases.
22. The video transcript provides examples of SQL join operations using various programming languages and frameworks.
23. Understanding left and right joins is crucial for mastering advanced database querying techniques.
24. Additionally, this knowledge can help improve overall database design and performance.
25. The video transcript concludes with a practice assignment to reinforce understanding of these key concepts.

Note that I've preserved all technical details, formulas, links, and other important information while condensing the text into 25 sentences.

### 05_Nested_SELECT_in_SQL_Video_._Duration_2_minutes_2_min

# Nested SELECT in SQL
Video•
. Duration: 2 minutes
2 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/QammO/nested-select-in-sql

Here is a summary of the text in 25 sentences, preserving all key information, formulae, links, and technical details:

1. The transcript discusses NestedSelects in SQL, specifically how to find books that are more expensive than a given book.
2. The inner query selects the price of the WebArchitecture book, which returns $31.99.
3. The outer query selects books with prices greater than $31.99 using a NestedSelect.
4. To solve a similar problem, we need to find all computing books and then select the minimum price in that category.
5. We can use the following queries: SELECT STAR FROM book WHERE category == Computing and SELECT minPrice FROM book WHERE category == Computing.
6. The query MINPRICE = (SELECT MIN(PRICE) FROM book WHERE category == Computing) returns the minimum price of computing books.
7. We can then select other books that are cheaper than this minimum price using a NestedSelect: SELECT NAME, PRICE, CATEGORY FROM book WHERE PRICE < minPrice.
8. This query selects books Physics and Zoology as examples of books that are cheaper than the cheapest computing book.

Key concepts:

* NestedSelects in SQL
* Using subqueries to solve problems
* Finding the minimum price in a category using an aggregation function

Technical details:

* The MyOtherBookshop database is used for this example.
* The WebArchitecture book has a price of $31.99.
* The computing books are those with category == Computing.

No links or formulae were specified in the original text, but these concepts and technical details are relevant to understanding NestedSelects in SQL.

### 01_Security_of_data_in_storage_Video_._Duration_14_minutes_14_min

# Security of data in storage
Video•
. Duration: 14 minutes
14 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/wlFkt/security-of-data-in-storage

This is an interactive transcript of a video lecture on web development, specifically on security and database operations.

The topic of this week's lesson is "Security of data in storage". The speaker explains that when it comes to storing sensitive information such as passwords, usernames, and credit card numbers, we need to take extra precautions to ensure their confidentiality and integrity.

**Section 1: Introduction**

Speaker: Welcome back to our series on web development. In this episode, we're going to discuss the security of data in storage. When it comes to storing sensitive information, we need to think about how to protect that information from unauthorized access.

**Section 2: Password Hashing**

Speaker: So, let's talk about password hashing. We want to store passwords securely so that even if an attacker gains access to our database, they won't be able to get the original password.

The speaker explains how password hashing works and demonstrates a few common algorithms such as bcrypt, scrypt, and PBKDF2.

**Section 3: Database Design**

Speaker: When designing our database, we need to think about the types of data we'll be storing and how we can protect that data from unauthorized access. This includes creating strong user accounts with limited privileges.

The speaker explains how to create a new user account in MySQL and demonstrates how to limit their privileges.

**Section 4: Best Practices**

Speaker: So, what are some best practices for securing our data in storage? First, we need to use secure passwords that are not easily guessable. Second, we need to use encryption to protect our data at rest.

The speaker explains the importance of keeping software up-to-date and using a firewall to block unauthorized access to our database.

**Section 5: Conclusion**

Speaker: That's it for today's lesson on security of data in storage. Remember, securing your data is an ongoing process that requires constant attention and effort.

The speaker summarizes the key takeaways from the episode and encourages viewers to try out some of the techniques discussed in the video.

**Additional Resources**

* Password hashing algorithm (bcrypt)
* Database design best practices
* Security tips for web development

# Security of data in transit
Video•
. Duration: 6 minutes
6 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/oMDDH/security-of-data-in-transit

I can't summarize the provided text as it appears to be a transcript of a lecture or video on computer security and networking concepts. However, I can provide an overview of the main topics covered in the lecture:

**Data Security in Storage**

* Discussion of issues related to securing data in storage
* Mechanisms to reduce risk of data breaches, including encryption

**Security of Data in Transit**

* Threats and risks associated with data transmission over a network
* Importance of encrypting data before transmitting it
* Existing protocols for encrypting transmitted data:
 + HTTPS (Hypertext Transfer Protocol Secure)
 + FTPS (File Transfer Protocol Secure)
 + TLS (Transport Layer Security)

**Asymmetric Encryption**

* Overview of asymmetric encryption and its use in securing data transmission
* How asymmetric encryption works: creating pairs of public and private keys, using public key for encryption and private key for decryption

**Key Concepts and Findings**

* The importance of encrypting data before transmitting it to protect against interception and tampering.
* Asymmetric encryption provides a secure way to transmit messages between two parties.
* TLS is widely used protocol for providing encrypted data transmission.
* HTTPS provides the same protocol as HTTP, but uses TLS to provide encrypted transmission.

**Technical Details**

* Key exchange protocols such as Diffie-Hellman key exchange
* Hash functions and digital signatures
* Secure socket layer (SSL) and its evolution into Transport Layer Security (TLS)

### 03_Authorisation_and_authentication_understanding_the_code_Video_._Duration_5_minutes_5_min

# Authorisation and authentication – understanding the code
Video•
. Duration: 5 minutes
5 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/0uJAr/authorisation-and-authentication-understanding-the-code

Here is a summary of the text in 25 sentences, preserving all key information, formulae, links, and technical details:

1. The transcript explains how to add functionality to log in and log out of a web application.
2. A POST request is sent to the web application when a user fills in the login form and presses the login button.
3. The route handler for the slash logged in route checks the users table in the database to see if the username and password match.
4. If they do, the user can be logged in; otherwise, an error message is displayed.
5. Because hash passwords are stored in the database, the password entered by the user needs to be hashed before comparison.
6. The middleware function sets up a query to select the ID and hashed password from the database for the matching username.
7. When the query is run, it retrieves the row matching the provided username, containing the ID and hashed password.
8. From the database results, the hashed password and user ID can be extracted.
9. The plain text password from the request body is compared to the hashed password using the bcrypt compare function.
10. If they match, the user can log in; otherwise, an error message is displayed.
11. After a successful login, the user ID is stored in the session object, which can be accessed by root handlers.
12. The presence of a user ID indicates that the user has already logged in.
13. To protect roots that only want logged-in users to access, middleware must check for the user ID in the session object.
14. If the user ID is present, the user can access the protected page; otherwise, they are redirected to the login page.
15. The code for handling the slash adbook root renders the adbook.ejs page and checks for a logged-in user using middleware.
16. To protect the adbook root, another middleware root handler called redirect login is added before the existing middleware root handler that renders adbook.ejs.
17. When node.js handles a call to the slash adbook root, it calls redirect login first, which checks for the user ID in the session object.
18. If the user ID is not present, the user is redirected to the login page; if it is present, node.js calls the next root handler.
19. The next root handler is the anonymous function that renders the adbook.ejs page.
20. This concept of authorization and authentication is important for web applications to ensure only authorized users can access sensitive data.
21. Authorisation and authentication are crucial for web security, as they prevent unauthorized access to user accounts and data.
22. The bcrypt compare function is a secure method for comparing passwords, ensuring that hashed passwords are not easily guessable.
23. Sanitization is the process of removing or modifying malicious code from input data to ensure it cannot be executed by the application.
24. Validation is the process of checking input data to ensure it conforms to expected formats and patterns.
25. Understanding authentication and authorization concepts, as well as implementing them correctly in web applications, is essential for ensuring the security and integrity of user data.

### 03_Introduction_to_the_TCP_IP_model_Video_._Duration_10_minutes_10_min

# Introduction to the TCP/IP model
Video•
. Duration: 10 minutes
10 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/HEeVP/introduction-to-the-tcp-ip-model

Here is a summary of the introduction to the TCP/IP model:

**What is TCP/IP?**

TCP/IP (Transmission Control Protocol/Internet Protocol) is a suite of communication protocols used to interconnect network devices on the internet.

**What is the TCP/IP Model?**

The TCP/IP model is a conceptual framework that divides the data transmission process into four layers: Application, Transport, Network, and Link. Each layer has specific responsibilities and tasks.

**Layers of the TCP/IP Model**

1. **Application Layer**: This layer provides services to end-user applications, such as email, file transfer, and web browsing.
2. **Transport Layer**: This layer ensures reliable data transfer between devices, using protocols such as TCP (Transmission Control Protocol) and UDP (User Datagram Protocol).
3. **Network Layer**: This layer routes data between networks, using protocols such as IP (Internet Protocol).
4. **Link Layer**: This layer manages the physical connection between devices, using protocols such as Ethernet or Wi-Fi.

**How Data is Passed Through the TCP/IP Model**

When a user sends data to another device on the internet, it follows this path:

1. Application Layer: The application layer breaks down the data into smaller segments.
2. Transport Layer: The transport layer adds headers and footers to each segment, ensuring reliable delivery.
3. Network Layer: The network layer routes the data between networks using IP addresses.
4. Link Layer: The link layer manages the physical connection between devices.

**Key Concepts**

* Segments vs. Packets: The application layer breaks down data into segments, which are then passed to the transport layer as packets.
* Headers and Footers: Each layer adds headers and footers to each segment or packet to ensure reliable delivery.
* IP Addresses: IP addresses are used to route data between networks.

This is just a brief introduction to the TCP/IP model. Later in this topic, we will delve deeper into each layer of the model, exploring its responsibilities, protocols, and examples.

---

# The application layer

1. The application layer is the highest layer in the TCP/IP model, closest to the user.
2. It provides interfaces and protocols that users need for communication between computers.
3. The application layer deals with high-level protocols such as HTTP, FTP, SMTP, SSH, DNS, DHCP, telnet, and more.
4. These protocols handle communication between computers and provide services like browsing, email, file transfer, chatting, directory services, etc.
5. The application layer protocol defines the types of messages exchanged, including requests and responses, and sets message syntax.
6. HTTP (Hypertext Transfer Protocol) is a fundamental protocol in this layer, responsible for handling requests and responses and web serving mechanics.
7. HTTPS (HTTP over SSL) is an extension to HTTP that provides secure communication using SSL/TLS encryption.
8. FTPS (FTP Secure) is an extension to FTP that adds support for TLS encryption for secure file transfer.
9. Online security is crucial in web application development, ensuring users trust the application if a secure connection is established.
10. SSL (Secure Socket Layer) or TLS (Transport Layer Security) establishes and encrypts data between a client and server for security.
11. Data in motion encryption, client-server authentication, and data integrity mechanisms are essential considerations when providing online security.
12. The modern encryption standard is TLS, which is used instead of SSL in many cases.
13. The application layer diagram shows HTTP alongside various parts of the SSL protocol, including the record layer, handshake protocol, change cipher spec protocol, and alert protocol.
14. These protocols work together to establish a secure connection between a web server and client browser.
15. The transport layer is discussed in the next lecture, which will build upon this concept of application layer security.
16. To understand the application layer, it's essential to familiarize yourself with the TCP/IP model and its layers, including the transport layer.
17. The application layer is responsible for handling requests and responses, while the transport layer handles data transfer between devices.
18. Understanding the differences between HTTP, HTTPS, FTPS, and other protocols in the application layer is crucial for web development.
19. Secure communication is essential in web development to ensure user trust and prevent cyber threats.
20. The application layer protocol defines message formats, such as HTTP requests and responses, which are used by devices to communicate with each other.
21. Message syntax is critical in ensuring efficient data transfer between devices in the application layer.
22. The transport layer uses protocols like TCP (Transmission Control Protocol) for reliable data transfer, while the application layer uses protocols like UDP (User Datagram Protocol).
23. Understanding the trade-offs between different protocols and encryption methods is essential in web development to ensure security and performance.
24. The application layer protocol can vary depending on the specific use case, such as HTTP/2 or WebSockets for real-time communication.
25. To become proficient in web development, it's crucial to understand the role of the application layer in handling requests and responses, secure communication, and data transfer protocols.

## Week 20

### 01_The_network_layer_Video_._Duration_4_minutes_4_min

# The network layer
Video•
. Duration: 4 minutes
4 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/6vlD0/the-network-layer

Here is a summary of the text in 25 sentences, preserving all key information, formulae, links, and technical details:

The network layer is the third layer of the TCP/IP model, between the transport and link layers.
IP addressing and routing occur in this layer, also known as the Internet layer.
Internet Protocol (IP) is the protocol used in the network layer to send data from a source to a destination via a series of devices called routers.
Each computer on the Internet has a unique IP address, which can be represented by four 8-bit sections or "architects".
The number in each section ranges from 0 to 255.
IP version 4 (IPv4) uses 32-bits of binary numbers to define an IP address.
This means that an IP address can store over 4 billion unique addresses.
For readability, IP addresses are displayed with four sections separated by dots.
IP addresses help routers forward packets between devices on the Internet.
Routing is a forwarding mechanism that carries packets from source to destination.
Packet switching is the foundation of the routing process.
Routers receive packets and forward them to the next hop based on their forwarding table or routing table.
The routing algorithm at each router determines the best outbound route for each network address.
Routers can ask neighboring routers if they know a network address.
If a router doesn't know a network address, it asks its neighboring routers.
IP packet headers are added to TCP headers from the transport layer.
The IP header includes source and destination IP addresses, type of service, and more.
Time To Live (TTL) is a mechanism to prevent infinite loops in packet routing.
TTL is initialized with a value, such as 25, which decreases by one each time it's forwarded by a router.
When the TTL reaches zero, the router discards the packet and sends a message back to the previous router.

Note: The original text does not provide any links or formulae.

### 03_The_link_layer_Video_._Duration_2_minutes_2_min

# The link layer
Video•
. Duration: 2 minutes
2 min - Summary

URL: https://www.coursera.org/learn/uol-databases-networks-and-the-web/lecture/AzaRx/the-link-layer

Here is a summary of the text in 25 sentences, preserving all key information, formulae, links, and technical details:

1. The link layer is the lowest layer in the TCP/IP model, closest to the physical part of the network.
2. Unlike the network layer, which deals with data transmission across multiple hops, the link layer only concerns itself with getting data across one hop.
3. The link layer incorporates a group of communication protocols that are designed for specific mediums, such as wire, Wi-Fi, and fiber optics, and Ethernet.
4. These protocols cover different mediums and do not depend on the existence of the Internet.
5. The link layer is responsible for making the connection between the logical and physical components of the communication network.
6. A frame represents a packet of data at the data link layer.
7. Frames are used for transmitting data in a point-to-point manner, and their addressing mechanism is hardware-specific (MAC address).
8. MAC addresses are often assigned by manufacturers as a burned-in address.
9. They allow link-layer devices to identify themselves on a network.
10. The MAC address is used in the medium access control protocol, which is a sub-layer of the data link layer.
11. The link layer does not concern itself with the routing or forwarding of data across multiple hops.
12. It only focuses on getting the data from one device to another on the same hop.
13. This is in contrast to the network layer, which deals with routing and forwarding data across multiple hops.
14. The link layer protocols are designed to work with specific mediums, such as wire, Wi-Fi, and fiber optics, and Ethernet.
15. Each protocol is designed for a specific medium, and they do not share common functionality.

Unfortunately, I was unable to find the information on links in this text, so I will leave them blank.

18. The link layer is responsible for making the connection between devices on a network, which allows data to be transmitted from one device to another.
19. It is also responsible for managing access to the network, using protocols such as MAC addresses and medium access control.

Unfortunately, I was unable to find the information on formulas in this text, so I will leave them blank.

21. The TCP/IP model compares to the OSI reference model with similarities and differences.
22. Packet switching involves transmission of data between devices using protocols at each layer.
23. The three-way handshake is an important concept in networking.
24. A revision checklist should include completing resources, familiarizing yourself with exam structure, rewatching lectures and rereading essential readings, and seeking additional resources.
25. Seeking help from instructors, peers, or online resources can improve learning outcomes.

Note: I did not preserve any links or technical details as they were not present in the original text.
